**James Abram Garfield** (November 19, 1831 – September 19, 1881) was the 20th [president of the United States](/wiki/President%5Fof%5Fthe%5FUnited%5FStates "President of the United States"), serving from March 1881 until [his assassination](/wiki/Assassination%5Fof%5FJames%5FA.%5FGarfield "Assassination of James A. Garfield") in September that year. A preacher, lawyer, and [Civil War](/wiki/American%5FCivil%5FWar "American Civil War") general, Garfield served nine terms in the [United States House of Representatives](/wiki/United%5FStates%5FHouse%5Fof%5FRepresentatives "United States House of Representatives") and is the only sitting member of the House to be elected president. Before his candidacy for the presidency, he had been elected to the [U.S. Senate](/wiki/U.S.%5FSenate "U.S. Senate") by the [Ohio General Assembly](/wiki/Ohio%5FGeneral%5FAssembly "Ohio General Assembly")—a position he declined when he became [president-elect](/wiki/President-elect%5Fof%5Fthe%5FUnited%5FStates "President-elect of the United States").

Garfield was born into poverty in a log cabin and grew up in [northeastern Ohio](/wiki/Northeast%5FOhio "Northeast Ohio"). After graduating from [Williams College](/wiki/Williams%5FCollege "Williams College") in 1856, he studied law and became an attorney. He was a preacher in the [Stone–Campbell Movement](/wiki/Stone%E2%80%93Campbell%5FMovement "Stone–Campbell Movement") and president of the [Western Reserve Eclectic Institute](/wiki/Western%5FReserve%5FEclectic%5FInstitute "Western Reserve Eclectic Institute"), affiliated with the [Disciples](/wiki/Christian%5FChurch%5F%28Disciples%5Fof%5FChrist%29 "Christian Church (Disciples of Christ)").[\[1\]](#cite%5Fnote-1)[\[a\]](#cite%5Fnote-3) Garfield was elected as a [Republican](/wiki/History%5Fof%5Fthe%5FRepublican%5FParty%5F%28United%5FStates%29 "History of the Republican Party (United States)") member of the [Ohio State Senate](/wiki/Ohio%5FState%5FSenate "Ohio State Senate") in 1859, serving until 1861\. He opposed [Confederate secession](/wiki/Confederate%5FStates%5Fof%5FAmerica "Confederate States of America"), was a [major general](/wiki/Major%5Fgeneral%5F%28United%5FStates%29 "Major general (United States)") in the [Union Army](/wiki/Union%5FArmy "Union Army") during the American Civil War, and fought in the battles of [Middle Creek](/wiki/Battle%5Fof%5FMiddle%5FCreek "Battle of Middle Creek"), [Shiloh](/wiki/Battle%5Fof%5FShiloh "Battle of Shiloh"), and [Chickamauga](/wiki/Battle%5Fof%5FChickamauga "Battle of Chickamauga"). He was elected to Congress in 1862 to represent [Ohio's 19th district](/wiki/Ohio%27s%5F19th%5Fcongressional%5Fdistrict "Ohio's 19th congressional district"). Throughout his congressional service, he firmly supported the [gold standard](/wiki/Gold%5Fstandard "Gold standard") and gained a reputation as a skilled orator. He initially agreed with [Radical Republican](/wiki/Radical%5FRepublican "Radical Republican") views on [Reconstruction](/wiki/Reconstruction%5Fera "Reconstruction era") but later favored a [Moderate Republican](/wiki/Moderate%5FRepublicans%5F%28Reconstruction%5Fera%29 "Moderate Republicans (Reconstruction era)")–aligned approach to civil rights enforcement for [freedmen](/wiki/Freedmen "Freedmen"). Garfield's aptitude for mathematics extended to [his own proof](/wiki/Garfield%27s%5Fproof%5Fof%5Fthe%5FPythagorean%5Ftheorem "Garfield's proof of the Pythagorean theorem") of the [Pythagorean theorem](/wiki/Pythagorean%5Ftheorem "Pythagorean theorem"), which he published in 1876.

At the [1880 Republican National Convention](/wiki/1880%5FRepublican%5FNational%5FConvention "1880 Republican National Convention"), delegates chose Garfield, who had not sought the White House, as a compromise presidential nominee on the 36th ballot. In the [1880 presidential election](/wiki/1880%5FUnited%5FStates%5Fpresidential%5Felection "1880 United States presidential election"), he conducted a low-key [front porch campaign](/wiki/Front%5Fporch%5Fcampaign "Front porch campaign") and narrowly defeated the Democratic nominee, [Winfield Scott Hancock](/wiki/Winfield%5FScott%5FHancock "Winfield Scott Hancock"). Garfield's accomplishments as president included his assertion of presidential authority against [senatorial courtesy](/wiki/Senatorial%5Fcourtesy "Senatorial courtesy") in executive appointments, a purge of corruption in the [Post Office](/wiki/United%5FStates%5FPost%5FOffice%5FDepartment "United States Post Office Department"), and his appointment of a Supreme Court justice. He advocated for [agricultural technology](/wiki/Agricultural%5Ftechnology "Agricultural technology"), an educated electorate, and [civil rights for African Americans](/wiki/Civil%5Frights%5Fmovement%5F%281865%E2%80%931896%29 "Civil rights movement (1865–1896)"). He also proposed substantial [civil service reforms](/wiki/Civil%5Fservice%5Freform%5Fin%5Fthe%5FUnited%5FStates "Civil service reform in the United States"), which were passed by Congress in 1883 as the [Pendleton Civil Service Reform Act](/wiki/Pendleton%5FCivil%5FService%5FReform%5FAct "Pendleton Civil Service Reform Act") and signed into law by his successor, [Chester A. Arthur](/wiki/Chester%5FA.%5FArthur "Chester A. Arthur").

Garfield was a member of the intraparty "[Half-Breed](/wiki/Half-Breeds%5F%28politics%29 "Half-Breeds (politics)")" faction who used the powers of the presidency to defy the powerful "[Stalwart](/wiki/Stalwarts%5F%28politics%29 "Stalwarts (politics)")" Senator [Roscoe Conkling](/wiki/Roscoe%5FConkling "Roscoe Conkling") from New York. He did this by appointing [Blaine faction](/wiki/Blaine%5Ffaction "Blaine faction") leader [William H. Robertson](/wiki/William%5FH.%5FRobertson "William H. Robertson") to the lucrative post of [Collector of the Port of New York](/wiki/Collector%5Fof%5Fthe%5FPort%5Fof%5FNew%5FYork "Collector of the Port of New York"). The ensuing political battle resulted in Robertson's confirmation and the resignations of Conkling and [Thomas C. Platt](/wiki/Thomas%5FC.%5FPlatt "Thomas C. Platt") from the Senate.

On July 2, 1881, [Charles J. Guiteau](/wiki/Charles%5FJ.%5FGuiteau "Charles J. Guiteau"), a disappointed and delusional [office seeker](/wiki/Spoils%5Fsystem "Spoils system"), shot Garfield at the [Baltimore and Potomac Railroad Station](/wiki/Baltimore%5Fand%5FPotomac%5FRailroad%5FStation "Baltimore and Potomac Railroad Station") in Washington. The wound was not immediately fatal, but an [infection caused by his doctors' unsanitary methods](/wiki/Iatrogenesis "Iatrogenesis") in treating the wound killed Garfield on September 19\. Due to his brief tenure in office, historians tend to [rank Garfield](/wiki/Historical%5Frankings%5Fof%5Fpresidents%5Fof%5Fthe%5FUnited%5FStates "Historical rankings of presidents of the United States") as a below-average president, though he has earned praise for anti-corruption and pro-civil rights stances.[\[3\]](#cite%5Fnote-4)
